       (the Confederacy). Led by
       <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Davis" title="Jefferson Davis">
        Jefferson Davis
       </a>
       , they fought against the
       <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">
        U.S. federal government (the Union)
       </a>
       under President
       <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">
        Abraham Lincoln
       </a>
       , which was supported by all the free states and the five
       <a href="/wiki/Border_states_(American_Civil_War)" title="Border states (American Civil War)">
        border slave states
       </a>
       in the north.
      </p>
      <p>
       Northern leaders agreed that victory would require more than the end of fighting. Secession and Confederate nationalism had to be totally repudiated and all forms of slavery or quasi-slavery had to be eliminated. Lincoln proved effective in mobilizing support for the war goals, raising large armies and supplying them, avoiding foreign interference, and making the end of slavery a war goal. The Confederacy had a larger area than it could defend, and it failed to keep its ports open and its rivers clear. The North kept up the pressure as the South could barely feed and clothe its soldiers. Its soldiers, especially those in the East under the command of General
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. Lee">
        Robert E. Lee
       </a>
       proved highly resourceful until they finally were overwhelmed by Generals Ulysses S. Grant and William T. Sherman in 1864–65, The Reconstruction Era (1863–77) began with the Emancipation proclamation in 1863, and included freedom, full citizenship and the vote for the Southern blacks. It was followed by a reaction that left the blacks in a second class status legally, politically, socially and economically until the 1960s.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Gilded_Age_and_legacy">
        The Gilded Age and legacy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: The Gilded Age and legacy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Gilded_Age" title="Gilded Age">
        Gilded Age
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the Gilded Age, there was substantial growth in population in the United States and extravagant displays of wealth and excess of America's upper-class during the post-Civil War and post-Reconstruction era, in the late 19th century. The wealth polarization derived primarily from industrial and population expansion. The businessmen of the Second Industrial Revolution created industrial towns and cities in the Northeast with new factories, and contributed to the creation of an ethnically diverse industrial
       <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">
        working class
       </a>
       which produced the wealth owned by rising super-rich
       <a href="/wiki/Robber_baron_(industrialist)" title="Robber baron (industrialist)">
        industrialists and financiers called the "robber barons"
       </a>
       . An example is the company of
       <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller" title="John D. Rockefeller">
        John D. Rockefeller
       </a>
       , who was an important figure in shaping the new oil industry. Using highly effective tactics and aggressive practices, later widely criticized,
       <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">
        Standard Oil
       </a>
       absorbed or destroyed most of its competition.
      </p>
      <p>
       The creation of a modern industrial economy took place. With the creation of a
       <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">
        transportation and communication infrastructure
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Corporation" title="Corporation">
        corporation
       </a>
       became the dominant form of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Business_organization" title="Business organization">
        business organization
       </a>
       and a
       <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">
        managerial revolution
       </a>
       transformed
       <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">
        business
       </a>
       operations. In 1890,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_United_States" title="Congress of the United States">
        Congress
       </a>
       passed the
       <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Antitrust_Act" title="Sherman Antitrust Act">
        Sherman Antitrust Act
       </a>
       —the source of all American anti-monopoly laws. The law forbade every contract, scheme, deal, or conspiracy to restrain trade, though the phrase "restraint of trade" remained subjective. By the beginning of the 20th century, per capita income and
       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_production" title="Industrial production">
        industrial production
       </a>
       in the United States exceeded that of any other country except Britain. Long hours and hazardous working conditions led many workers to attempt to form
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labor_union" title="Labor union">
        labor unions
       </a>
       despite strong opposition from industrialists and the courts. But the courts did protect the marketplace, declaring the Standard Oil group to be an "unreasonable"
       <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">
        monopoly
       </a>
       under the Sherman Antitrust Act in 1911. It ordered Standard to break up into 34 independent companies with different boards of directors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_philosophy">
        Science and philosophy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Science and philosophy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Replacing the
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_physics" title="Classical physics">
        classical physics
       </a>
       in use since the end of the scientific revolution,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Modern_physics" title="Modern physics">
         modern physics
        </a>
       </i>
       arose in the early 20th century with the advent of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quantum_physics" title="Quantum physics">
        quantum physics
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       substituting
       <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_physics" title="Mathematical physics">
        mathematical studies
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/Experimental_physics" title="Experimental physics">
        experimental studies
       </a>
       and examining
       <a href="/wiki/Equation" title="Equation">
        equations
       </a>
       to build a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theoretical_structure" title="Theoretical structure">
        theoretical structure
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="Characterizing modern physics as substituting theory for experiment is an incredible claim. (August 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Old_quantum_theory" title="Old quantum theory">
        old quantum theory
       </a>
       was a collection of results which predate modern
       <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">
        quantum mechanics
       </a>
       , but were never complete or self-consistent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HaarQM_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HaarQM-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The collection of
       <a href="/wiki/Heuristic" title="Heuristic">
        heuristic
       </a>
       prescriptions for quantum mechanics were the first corrections to
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_mechanics" title="Classical mechanics">
        classical mechanics
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HaarQM_78-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-HaarQM-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Outside the realm of quantum physics, the various
       <a href="/wiki/Aether_theories" title="Aether theories">
        aether theories
       </a>
       in classical physics, which supposed a "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_elements" title="Classical elements">
        fifth element
       </a>
       " such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Luminiferous_aether" title="Luminiferous aether">
        Luminiferous aether
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       were nullified by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michelson-Morley_experiment" title="Michelson-Morley experiment">
        Michelson-Morley experiment
       </a>
       —an attempt to detect the motion of earth through the aether. In biology,
       <a href="/wiki/Darwinism" title="Darwinism">
        Darwinism
       </a>
       gained acceptance, promoting the concept of
       <a href="/wiki/Adaptation" title="Adaptation">
        adaptation
       </a>
       in the theory of
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">
        natural selection
       </a>
       . The fields of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_geology" title="Modern geology">
        geology
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_astronomy" title="Modern astronomy">
        astronomy
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_psychology" title="Modern psychology">
        psychology
       </a>
       also made strides and gained new insights. In
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_medicine" title="Modern medicine">
        medicine
       </a>
       , there were advances in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_theory" title="Medical theory">
        medical theory
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_treatment" title="Medical treatment">
        treatments
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="639" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg/220px-Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg/330px-Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg/440px-Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Xinhai_Revolution_in_Shanghai.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">
          Xinhai Revolution
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">
          Shanghai
         </a>
         ;
         <a href="/wiki/Chen_Qimei" title="Chen Qimei">
          Chen Qimei
         </a>
         organized Shanghainese civilians to start the uprising and was successful. The picture above is
         <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Road" title="Nanjing Road">
          Nanjing Road
         </a>
         after the uprising, hung with the
         <a href="/wiki/Five_Races_Under_One_Union" title="Five Races Under One Union">
          Five Races Under One Union
         </a>
         Flags then used by the revolutionaries.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The assertions of Chinese philosophy
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       began to integrate concepts of Western philosophy, as steps toward modernization. By the time of the
       <a href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">
        Xinhai Revolution
       </a>
       in 1911, there were many calls, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/May_Fourth_Movement" title="May Fourth Movement">
        May Fourth Movement
       </a>
       , to completely abolish the old imperial institutions and practices of China. There were attempts to incorporate
       <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">
        democracy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">
        republicanism
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrialism" title="Industrialism">
        industrialism
       </a>
       into Chinese philosophy, notably by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-Sen" title="Sun Yat-Sen">
        Sun Yat-Sen
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Sūn yì xiān
       </i>
       , in one Mandarin form of the name) at the beginning of the 20th century.
       <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">
        Mao Zedong
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Máo zé dōng
       </i>
       ) added
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxism-Leninism" title="Marxism-Leninism">
        Marxist-Leninist
       </a>
       thought. When the
       <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">
        Communist Party of China
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">
        took over
       </a>
       power, previous schools of thought, excepting notably
       <a href="/wiki/Legalism_(Chinese_philosophy)" title="Legalism (Chinese philosophy)">
        Legalism
       </a>
       , were denounced as backward, and later even purged during the
       <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">
        Cultural Revolution
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Starting one-hundred years before the 20th century, the
       <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_(spiritual)" title="Enlightenment (spiritual)">
        enlightenment spiritual philosophy
       </a>
       was challenged in various quarters around the 1900s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Developed from earlier
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secular" title="Secular">
        secular
       </a>
       traditions,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       modern
       <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">
        Humanist
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Ethics" title="Ethics">
        ethical philosophies
       </a>
       affirmed the dignity and worth of all people, based on the ability to determine right and wrong by appealing to universal human qualities, particularly
       <a href="/wiki/Rationalism" title="Rationalism">
        rationality
       </a>
       , without resorting to the supernatural or alleged divine authority from religious texts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberal_humanism" title="Liberal humanism">
        liberal humanists
       </a>
       such as
       <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau" title="Jean-Jacques Rousseau">
        Rousseau
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Kant" title="Immanuel Kant">
        Kant
       </a>
       , the universal law of
       <a href="/wiki/Reason" title="Reason">
        reason
       </a>
       guided the way toward total emancipation from any kind of tyranny. These ideas were challenged, for example by the
       <a href="/wiki/Young_Marx" title="Young Marx">
        young Karl Marx
       </a>
       , who criticized the project of political emancipation (embodied in the form of
       <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">
        human rights
       </a>
       ), asserting it to be symptomatic of the very dehumanization it was supposed to oppose. For
       <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Nietzsche" title="Friedrich Nietzsche">
        Friedrich Nietzsche
       </a>
       , humanism was nothing more than a secular version of
       <a href="/wiki/Theism" title="Theism">
        theism
       </a>
       . In his
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genealogy_of_Morals" title="Genealogy of Morals">
         Genealogy of Morals
        </a>
       </i>
       , he argues that human rights exist as a means for the weak to collectively constrain the strong. On this view, such rights do not facilitate emancipation of life, but rather deny it. In the 20th century, the notion that human beings are rationally autonomous was challenged by the concept that humans were driven by unconscious irrational desires.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_persons">
        Notable persons
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Notable persons">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Sigmund_Freud" title="Sigmund Freud">
        Sigmund Freud
       </a>
       is renowned for his redefinition of
       <a href="/wiki/Sexual_desire" title="Sexual desire">
        sexual desire
       </a>
       as the primary motivational energy of human life, as well as his therapeutic techniques, including the use of
       <a href="/wiki/Free_association_(psychology)" title="Free association (psychology)">
        free association
       </a>
       , his
       <a href="/wiki/Transference" title="Transference">
        theory of transference
       </a>
       in the therapeutic relationship, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Dream_interpretation" title="Dream interpretation">
        interpretation of dreams
       </a>
       as sources of insight into
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unconscious_desire" title="Unconscious desire">
        unconscious desires
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">
        Albert Einstein
       </a>
       is known for his theories of
       <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">
        special relativity
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">
        general relativity
       </a>
       . He also made important contributions to
       <a href="/wiki/Statistical_mechanics" title="Statistical mechanics">
        statistical mechanics
       </a>
       , especially his mathematical treatment of
       <a href="/wiki/Brownian_motion" title="Brownian motion">
        Brownian motion
       </a>
       , his resolution of the
       <a href="/wiki/Einstein_solid" title="Einstein solid">
        paradox of specific heats
       </a>
       , and his connection of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fluctuation_dissipation_theorem" title="Fluctuation dissipation theorem">
        fluctuations and dissipation
       </a>
       . Despite his reservations about its interpretation, Einstein also made contributions to quantum mechanics and, indirectly,
       <a href="/wiki/Quantum_field_theory" title="Quantum field theory">
        quantum field theory
       </a>
       , primarily through his theoretical studies of the
       <a href="/wiki/Photon" title="Photon">
        photon
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Social_Darwinism">
        Social Darwinism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Social Darwinism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       At the end of the 19th century,
       <a href="/wiki/Social_Darwinism" title="Social Darwinism">
        Social Darwinism
       </a>
       was promoted and included the various ideologies based on a concept that competition among all individuals, groups, nations, or ideas was a "natural" framework for social evolution in human societies. In this view, society's advancement is dependent on the "
       <a href="/wiki/Survival_of_the_fittest" title="Survival of the fittest">
        survival of the fittest
       </a>
       ", the term was in fact coined by
       <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Spencer" title="Herbert Spencer">
        Herbert Spencer
       </a>
       and referred to in "
       <a href="/wiki/The_Gospel_of_Wealth" title="The Gospel of Wealth">
        The Gospel of Wealth
       </a>
       " written by
       <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">
        Andrew Carnegie
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Marxist_society">
        Marxist society
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Marxist society">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Communist-manifesto.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1045" data-file-width="600" height="383" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Communist-manifesto.png/220px-Communist-manifesto.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Communist-manifesto.png/330px-Communist-manifesto.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Communist-manifesto.png/440px-Communist-manifesto.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Communist-manifesto.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          The Communist Manifesto
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">
        Karl Marx
       </a>
       summarized his approach to history and politics in the opening line of the first chapter of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Communist_Manifesto" title="The Communist Manifesto">
         The Communist Manifesto
        </a>
       </i>
       (1848). He wrote:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         The history of all hitherto existing society is the history of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_struggle" title="Class struggle">
          class struggles
         </a>
         .
        </i>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
         <a href="#cite_note-91">
          [91]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        Manifesto
       </i>
       went through a number of editions from 1872 to 1890; notable new prefaces were written by Marx and Engels for the 1872 German edition, the 1882 Russian edition, the 1883 German edition, and the 1888 English edition. In general,
       <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">
        Marxism
       </a>
       identified five (and one transitional) successive stages of development in Western Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primitive_Communism" title="Primitive Communism">
         Primitive Communism
        </a>
        : as seen in cooperative tribal societies.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave" title="Slave">
         Slave
        </a>
        Society: which develops when the tribe becomes a city-state. Aristocracy is born.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">
         Feudalism
        </a>
        : aristocracy is the ruling class. Merchants develop into capitalists.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">
         Capitalism
        </a>
        : capitalists are the ruling class, who create and employ the true working class.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship_of_the_proletariat" title="Dictatorship of the proletariat">
         Dictatorship of the proletariat
        </a>
        : workers gain class consciousness,
        <a href="/wiki/Proletarian_revolution" title="Proletarian revolution">
         overthrow
        </a>
        the capitalists and take control over the
        <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">
         state
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">
         Communism
        </a>
        : a
        <a href="/wiki/Classless_society" title="Classless society">
         classless
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Stateless_society" title="Stateless society">
         stateless society
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ol>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="European_decline_and_the_20th_century">
        European decline and the 20th century
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: European decline and the 20th century">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/20th_century" title="20th century">
        20th century
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Major political developments saw the former
       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
        British Empire
       </a>
       lose most of its remaining political power over
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Commonwealth" title="British Commonwealth">
        commonwealth
       </a>
       countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">
        Trans-Siberian Railway
       </a>
       , crossing Asia by train, was complete by 1916. Other events include the
       <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli–Palestinian conflict">
        Israeli–Palestinian conflict
       </a>
       , two world wars, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">
        Cold War
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Australian_Constitution">
        Australian Constitution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Australian Constitution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       In 1901, the
       <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Australia" title="Federation of Australia">
        Federation of Australia
       </a>
       was the process by which the six separate British
       <a href="/wiki/Self-governing_colony" title="Self-governing colony">
        self-governing colonies
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">
        New South Wales
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">
        Queensland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">
        South Australia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">
        Tasmania
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">
        Victoria
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">
        Western Australia
       </a>
       formed one nation. They kept the systems of government that they had developed as separate colonies but also would have a federal government that was responsible for matters concerning the whole nation. When the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Australia" title="Constitution of Australia">
        Constitution of Australia
       </a>
       came into force, the colonies collectively became
       <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">
        states
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">
        Commonwealth of Australia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_warlords">
        Eastern warlords
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Eastern warlords">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The last days of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" title="Qing Dynasty">
        Qing Dynasty
       </a>
       were marked by civil unrest and foreign invasions. Responding to these civil failures and discontent, the Qing Imperial Court did attempt to reform the government in various ways, such as the decision to draft a constitution in 1906, the establishment of provincial legislatures in 1909, and the preparation for a national parliament in 1910. However, many of these measures were opposed by the conservatives of the Qing Court, and many reformers were either imprisoned or executed outright. The failures of the Imperial Court to enact such reforming measures of political liberalization and modernization caused the reformists to steer toward the road of revolution.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1912, the Republic of China was established and Sun Yat-sen was inaugurated in
       <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">
        Nanjing
       </a>
       as the first
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="President of the Republic of China">
        Provisional President
       </a>
       . But power in
       <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">
        Beijing
       </a>
       already had passed to
       <a href="/wiki/Yuan_Shikai" title="Yuan Shikai">
        Yuan Shikai
       </a>
       , who had effective control of the
       <a href="/wiki/Beiyang_Army" title="Beiyang Army">
        Beiyang Army
       </a>
       , the most powerful military force in China at the time. To prevent
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_war" title="Civil war">
        civil war
       </a>
       and possible foreign intervention from undermining the infant republic, leaders agreed to Army's demand that China be united under a Beijing government. On March 10, in Beijing, Shikai was sworn in as the second Provisional President of the Republic of China.
      </p>
      <p>
       After the early 20th century revolutions, shifting alliances of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warlord_era_(China)" title="Warlord era (China)">
        China's regional warlords
       </a>
       waged war for control of the Beijing government. Despite the fact that various warlords gained control of the government in Beijing during the warlord era, this did not constitute a new era of control or governance, because other warlords did not acknowledge the transitory governments in this period and were a law unto themselves. These military-dominated governments were collectively known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Beiyang_government" title="Beiyang government">
        Beiyang government
       </a>
       . The warlord era ended around 1927.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="World_Wars_era">
        World Wars era
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: World Wars era">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_World_War_I" title="Timeline of World War I">
        Timeline of World War I
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_World_War_II" title="Timeline of World War II">
        Timeline of World War II
       </a>
      </div>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Start_of_the_20th_century">
        Start of the 20th century
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Start of the 20th century">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <p>
       Four years into the 20th century saw the
       <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">
        Russo-Japanese War
       </a>
       with the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Port_Arthur" title="Battle of Port Arthur">
        Battle of Port Arthur
       </a>
       establishing the
       <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">
        Empire of Japan
       </a>
       as a world power. The Russians were in constant pursuit of a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warm_water_port" title="Warm water port">
        warm water port
       </a>
       on the Pacific Ocean, for their navy as well as for maritime trade. The Manchurian Campaign of the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
        Russian Empire
       </a>
       was fought against the Japanese over
       <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">
        Manchuria
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">
        Korea
       </a>
       . The major theatres of operations were Southern Manchuria, specifically the area around the
       <a href="/wiki/Liaodong_Peninsula" title="Liaodong Peninsula">
        Liaodong Peninsula
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mukden" title="Mukden">
        Mukden
       </a>
       , and the seas around Korea, Japan, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Sea" title="Yellow Sea">
        Yellow Sea
       </a>
       . The resulting campaigns, in which the fledgling Japanese military consistently attained victory over the Russian forces arrayed against them, were unexpected by world observers. These victories, as time transpired, would dramatically transform the distribution of power in East Asia, resulting in a reassessment of Japan's recent entry onto the world stage. The embarrassing string of defeats increased Russian popular dissatisfaction with the inefficient and corrupt Tsarist government.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_of_1905" title="Russian Revolution of 1905">
        Russian Revolution of 1905
       </a>
       was a wave of mass political unrest through vast areas of the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
        Russian Empire
       </a>
       . Some of it was directed against the government, while some was undirected. It included
       <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">
        terrorism
       </a>
       , worker strikes, peasant unrests, and military mutinies. It led to the establishment of the limited constitutional monarchy,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the establishment of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Duma_of_the_Russian_Empire" title="State Duma of the Russian Empire">
        State Duma of the Russian Empire
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">
        multi-party system
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In China, the Qing Dynasty was overthrown following the
       <a href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">
        Xinhai Revolution
       </a>
       . The
       <i>
        Xinhai Revolution
       </i>
       began with the
       <a href="/wiki/Wuchang_Uprising" title="Wuchang Uprising">
        Wuchang Uprising
       </a>
       on October 10, 1911 and ended with the abdication of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emperor_Puyi" title="Emperor Puyi">
        Emperor Puyi
       </a>
       on February 12, 1912. The primary parties to the conflict were the Imperial forces of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" title="Qing Dynasty">
        Qing Dynasty
       </a>
       (1644–1911), and the revolutionary forces of the
       <a href="/wiki/Tongmenghui" title="Tongmenghui">
        Chinese Revolutionary Alliance
       </a>
       (Tongmenghui).
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Edwardian_Britain">
        Edwardian Britain
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Edwardian Britain">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Edwardian_era" title="Edwardian era">
        Edwardian era
       </a>
       in the United Kingdom is the period spanning the reign of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_VII_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Edward VII of the United Kingdom">
        King Edward VII
       </a>
       up to the end of the First World War, including the years surrounding the sinking of the
       <a href="/wiki/RMS_Titanic" title="RMS Titanic">
        RMS
        <i>
         Titanic
        </i>
       </a>
       . In the early years of the period, the
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">
        Second Boer War
       </a>
       in South Africa split the country into anti- and pro-war factions. The imperial policies of the Conservatives eventually proved unpopular and in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1906" title="United Kingdom general election, 1906">
        general election of 1906
       </a>
       the Liberals won a huge landslide. The Liberal government was unable to proceed with all of its radical programme without the support of the
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">
        House of Lords
       </a>
       , which was largely Conservative. Conflict between the two Houses of Parliament over the
       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Budget" title="People's Budget">
        People's Budget
       </a>
       led to a reduction in the power of the peers in 1910. The
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_January_1910" title="United Kingdom general election, January 1910">
        general election in January that year
       </a>
       returned a
       <a href="/wiki/Hung_parliament" title="Hung parliament">
        hung parliament
       </a>
       with the balance of power held by
       <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">
        Labour
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Party_(Ireland)" title="Nationalist Party (Ireland)">
        Irish Nationalist
       </a>
       members.
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">
        World War I
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: World War I">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Causes_of_World_War_I" title="Causes of World War I">
        causes of World War I
       </a>
       included many factors, including the conflicts and antagonisms of the four decades leading up to the war. The
       <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">
        Triple Entente
       </a>
       was the name given to the loose alignment between the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">
        France
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
        Russia
       </a>
       after the signing of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Russian_Entente" title="Anglo-Russian Entente">
        Anglo-Russian Entente
       </a>
       in 1907. The alignment of the three powers, supplemented by various agreements with
       <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">
        Japan
       </a>
       , the United States, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spain_under_the_Restoration" title="Spain under the Restoration">
        Spain
       </a>
       , constituted a powerful counterweight to the
       <a href="/wiki/Triple_Alliance_(1882)" title="Triple Alliance (1882)">
        Triple Alliance
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">
        Germany
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">
        Austria-Hungary
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(1861%E2%80%931946)" title="Kingdom of Italy (1861–1946)">
        Italy
       </a>
       , the third having concluded an additional secret agreement with France effectively nullifying her Alliance commitments. Militarism, alliances, imperialism, and nationalism played major roles in the conflict. The immediate origins of the war lay in the decisions taken by statesmen and generals during the
       <a href="/wiki/July_Crisis" title="July Crisis">
        July Crisis
       </a>
       of 1914, the spark (or casus belli) for which was the assassination of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archduke_Franz_Ferdinand" title="Archduke Franz Ferdinand">
        Archduke Franz Ferdinand
       </a>
       of Austria.
      </p>
      <p>
       However, the crisis did not exist in a void; it came after a long series of diplomatic clashes between the Great Powers over European and colonial issues in the decade prior to 1914 which had left tensions high. The diplomatic clashes can be traced to changes in the balance of power in Europe since 1870. An example is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baghdad_Railway" title="Baghdad Railway">
        Baghdad Railway
       </a>
       which was planned to connect the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Konya" title="Konya">
        Konya
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">
        Baghdad
       </a>
       with a line through modern-day Turkey, Syria and Iraq. The railway became a source of international disputes during the years immediately preceding World War I. Although it has been argued that they were resolved in 1914 before the war began, it has also been argued that the railroad was a cause of the First World War.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Fundamentally the war was sparked by tensions over territory in the
       <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">
        Balkans
       </a>
       . Austria-Hungary competed with Serbia and Russia for territory and influence in the region and they pulled the rest of the great powers into the conflict through their various alliances and treaties. The
       <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">
        Balkan Wars
       </a>
       were two wars in South-eastern Europe in 1912–1913 in the course of which the
       <a href="/wiki/Balkan_League" title="Balkan League">
        Balkan League
       </a>
       (Bulgaria, Montenegro, Greece, and Serbia) first captured Ottoman-held remaining part of Thessaly, Macedonia, Epirus, Albania and most of Thrace and then fell out over the division of the spoils, with incorporation of Romania this time.
      </p>
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World_War_1.gif">
          <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" height="347" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/World_War_1.gif/750px-World_War_1.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/World_War_1.gif/1125px-World_War_1.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e4/World_War_1.gif 2x" width="750"/>
         </a>
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World_War_1.gif" title="Enlarge">
           </a>
          </div>
          Various periods of World War I; 1914.07.28 (Tsar Nicholas II of Russia orders a partial mobilization against Austria-Hungary), 1914.08.01 (Germany declares war on Russia), 1914.08.03 (Germany declares war on Russia's ally France), 1914.08.04 (Britain declares war on Germany), 1914.12 (British and German
          <a href="/wiki/Christmas_truce" title="Christmas truce">
           Christmas truce
          </a>
          ), 1915.12 (French and German Christmas truce), 1916.12 (
          <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Magdhaba" title="Battle of Magdhaba">
           Battle of Magdhaba
          </a>
          ), 1917.12 (British troops take Jerusalem from the Ottoman Empire), and 1918.11.11 (World War I ends: Germany signs an armistice agreement with the Allies).
          <hr/>
          Allies and Central Powers in the First World War
          <br/>
          <span style="background-color:#088A08; color:black; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          <span style="background-color:#01DF01; color:black; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Allied powers and areas
          <br/>
          <span style="background-color:#FE9A2E; color:black; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          <span style="background-color:#F7BE81; color:black; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Central powers and colonies or occupied territory
          <br/>
          <span style="background-color:#BDBDBD; color:black; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Neutral countries
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The First World War began in 1914 and lasted to the final
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armistice_with_Germany_(Compi%C3%A8gne)" title="Armistice with Germany (Compiègne)">
        Armistice
       </a>
       in 1918. The
       <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">
        Allied Powers
       </a>
       , led by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Britain_in_World_War_I" title="Britain in World War I">
        British Empire
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">
        France
       </a>
       , Russia until March 1918, Japan and the United States after 1917, defeated the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">
        Central Powers
       </a>
       , led by the
       <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">
        German Empire
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">
        Austro-Hungarian Empire
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       . The war caused the disintegration of four empires—the Austro-Hungarian, German, Ottoman, and Russian ones—as well as radical change in the European and West Asian maps. The Allied powers before 1917 are referred to as the
       <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">
        Triple Entente
       </a>
       , and the Central Powers are referred to as the
       <a href="/wiki/Triple_Alliance_(1882)" title="Triple Alliance (1882)">
        Triple Alliance
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Much of the fighting in World War I took place along the
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">
        Western Front
       </a>
       , within a system of opposing manned trenches and fortifications (separated by a "
       <a href="/wiki/No_man%27s_land" title="No man's land">
        No man's land
       </a>
       ") running from the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">
        North Sea
       </a>
       to the border of Switzerland. On the
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Eastern Front (World War I)">
        Eastern Front
       </a>
       , the vast eastern plains and limited rail network prevented a trench warfare stalemate from developing, although the scale of the conflict was just as large. Hostilities also occurred on and under the sea and—for the first time—from the air. More than 9 million soldiers died on the various battlefields, and nearly that many more in the participating countries' home fronts on account of food shortages and
       <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
        genocide
       </a>
       committed under the cover of various civil wars and internal conflicts. Notably, more people died of the worldwide
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_flu" title="Spanish flu">
        influenza outbreak
       </a>
       at the end of the war and shortly after than died in the hostilities. The unsanitary conditions engendered by the war, severe overcrowding in barracks, wartime propaganda interfering with public health warnings, and migration of so many soldiers around the world helped the outbreak become a
       <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">
        pandemic
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Ultimately, World War I created a decisive break with the old
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_World_Order_(political)" title="New World Order (political)">
        world order
       </a>
       that had emerged after the
       <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">
        Napoleonic Wars
       </a>
       , which was modified by the mid-19th century's nationalistic revolutions. The results of World War I would be important factors in the development of World War II approximately 20 years later. More immediate to the time, the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Partitioning_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Partitioning of the Ottoman Empire">
         partitioning of the Ottoman Empire
        </a>
       </i>
       was a political event that redrew the political boundaries of West Asia. The huge conglomeration of territories and peoples formerly ruled by the Sultan of the Ottoman Empire was divided into several new nations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The partitioning brought the creation of the modern
       <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">
        Arab world
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Turkey" title="Republic of Turkey">
        Republic of Turkey
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
        League of Nations
       </a>
       granted France mandates over
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Mandate_of_Syria" title="French Mandate of Syria">
        Syria
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Mandate_of_Lebanon" title="French Mandate of Lebanon">
        Lebanon
       </a>
       and granted the United Kingdom mandates over
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Mandate_of_Mesopotamia" title="British Mandate of Mesopotamia">
        Mesopotamia
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Mandate_of_Palestine" title="British Mandate of Palestine">
        Palestine
       </a>
       (which was later divided into two regions:
       <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">
        Palestine
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan" title="Emirate of Transjordan">
        Transjordan
       </a>
       ). Parts of the Ottoman Empire on the
       <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">
        Arabian Peninsula
       </a>
       became parts of what are today
       <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">
        Saudi Arabia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">
        Yemen
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Revolutions_and_war">
        Revolutions and war
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Revolutions and war">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">
        Russian Revolution
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">
        Russian Civil War
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         National flag of the Soviet Union.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Russian Revolution is the series of revolutions in Russia in 1917, which destroyed the
       <a href="/wiki/Tsarist_autocracy" title="Tsarist autocracy">
        Tsarist autocracy
       </a>
       and led to the creation of the Soviet Union. Following the abdication of
       <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">
        Nicholas II of Russia
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Provisional_Government" title="Russian Provisional Government">
        Russian Provisional Government
       </a>
       was established. In October 1917, a
       <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">
        <i>
         red
        </i>
        faction revolution
       </a>
       occurred in which the
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Guards_(Russia)" title="Red Guards (Russia)">
        Red Guard
       </a>
       , armed groups of workers and deserting soldiers directed by the Bolshevik Party, seized control of
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">
        Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       (then known as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrograd" title="Petrograd">
        Petrograd
       </a>
       ) and began an immediate armed takeover of cities and villages throughout the former
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
        Russian Empire
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Another action in 1917 that is of note was the armistice signed between Russia and the Central Powers at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brest-Litovsk" title="Brest-Litovsk">
        Brest-Litovsk
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a condition for peace, the treaty by the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">
        Central Powers
       </a>
       conceded huge portions of the former Russian Empire to
       <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">
        Imperial Germany
       </a>
       and the Ottoman Empire, greatly upsetting
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nationalist" title="Nationalist">
        nationalists
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Conservatism" title="Conservatism">
        conservatives
       </a>
       . The Bolsheviks made peace with the
       <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">
        German Empire
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">
        Central Powers
       </a>
       , as they had promised the Russian people prior to the Revolution. Vladimir Lenin's decision has been attributed to his sponsorship by the foreign office of
       <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_II,_German_Emperor" title="Wilhelm II, German Emperor">
        Wilhelm II, German Emperor
       </a>
       , offered by the latter in hopes that with a revolution, Russia would withdraw from World War I. This suspicion was bolstered by the German Foreign Ministry's sponsorship of Lenin's return to
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">
        Petrograd
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">
        Western Allies
       </a>
       expressed their dismay at the Bolsheviks, upset at:
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        the withdrawal of Russia from the war effort,
       </li>
       <li>
        worried about a possible Russo-German alliance, and
       </li>
       <li>
        galvanized by the prospect of the Bolsheviks making good their threats to assume no responsibility for, and so default on, Imperial Russia's massive
        <a href="/wiki/External_debt" title="External debt">
         foreign loans
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
         <a href="#cite_note-100">
          [100]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       In addition, there was a concern, shared by many
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">
        Central Powers
       </a>
       as well, that the socialist revolutionary ideas would spread to the West. Hence, many of these countries expressed their support for the Whites, including the provision of troops and supplies.
       <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">
        Winston Churchill
       </a>
       declared that Bolshevism must be "strangled in its cradle".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Russian Civil War was a multi-party war that occurred within the former
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
        Russian Empire
       </a>
       after the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_provisional_government" title="Russian provisional government">
        Russian provisional government
       </a>
       collapsed and the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_republic_(system_of_government)" title="Soviet republic (system of government)">
        Soviets
       </a>
       under the domination of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshevik" title="Bolshevik">
        Bolshevik
       </a>
       party assumed power, first in
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">
        Petrograd (St. Petersburg)
       </a>
       and then in other places. In the wake of the
       <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">
        October Revolution
       </a>
       , the old Russian Imperial Army had been demobilized; the volunteer-based Red Guard was the Bolsheviks' main military force, augmented by an armed military component of the
       <a href="/wiki/Cheka" title="Cheka">
        Cheka
       </a>
       , the Bolshevik state security apparatus. There was an instituted mandatory conscription of the rural peasantry into the Red Army.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Opposition of rural Russians to Red Army conscription units was overcome by taking hostages and shooting them when necessary in order to force compliance.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Former Tsarist officers were utilized as "military specialists" (
       <i>
        voenspetsy
       </i>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       taking their families hostage in order to ensure loyalty.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams,_Beryl_1921_105-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Williams,_Beryl_1921-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At the start of the war, three-fourths of the Red Army officer corps was composed of former Tsarist officers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams,_Beryl_1921_105-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Williams,_Beryl_1921-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By its end, 83% of all Red Army divisional and corps commanders were ex-Tsarist soldiers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The principal fighting occurred between the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshevik" title="Bolshevik">
        Bolshevik
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">
        Red Army
       </a>
       and the forces of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Movement" title="White Movement">
        White Army
       </a>
       . Many foreign armies warred against the Red Army, notably the
       <a href="/wiki/Allied_intervention_in_the_Russian_Civil_War" title="Allied intervention in the Russian Civil War">
        Allied Forces
       </a>
       , yet many volunteer foreigners fought in both sides of the Russian Civil War. Other nationalist and regional political groups also participated in the war, including the Ukrainian nationalist
       <a href="/wiki/Green_armies" title="Green armies">
        Green Army
       </a>
       , the Ukrainian anarchist
       <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Insurrectionary_Army_of_Ukraine" title="Revolutionary Insurrectionary Army of Ukraine">
        Black Army
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Black_Guards" title="Black Guards">
        Black Guards
       </a>
       , and warlords such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ungern_von_Sternberg" title="Ungern von Sternberg">
        Ungern von Sternberg
       </a>
       . The most intense fighting took place from 1918 to 1920. Major military operations ended on 25 October 1922 when the Red Army occupied
       <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">
        Vladivostok
       </a>
       , previously held by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Provisional_Priamur_Government" title="Provisional Priamur Government">
        Provisional Priamur Government
       </a>
       . The last enclave of the White Forces was the
       <a href="/wiki/Ayano-Maysky_District" title="Ayano-Maysky District">
        Ayano-Maysky District
       </a>
       on the Pacific coast. The majority of the fighting ended in 1920 with the defeat of General
       <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Wrangel" title="Pyotr Wrangel">
        Pyotr Wrangel
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">
        Crimea
       </a>
       , but a notable resistance in certain areas continued until 1923 (e.g.,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kronstadt_Uprising" title="Kronstadt Uprising">
        Kronstadt Uprising
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tambov_Rebellion" title="Tambov Rebellion">
        Tambov Rebellion
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basmachi_Revolt" title="Basmachi Revolt">
        Basmachi Revolt
       </a>
       , and the final resistance of the
       <a href="/wiki/White_movement" title="White movement">
        White movement
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">
        Far East
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1917, China declared war on Germany in the hope of recovering its lost province, then under Japanese control. The
       <a href="/wiki/New_Culture_Movement" title="New Culture Movement">
        New Culture Movement
       </a>
       occupied the period from 1917 to 1923. Chinese representatives refused to sign the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">
        Treaty of Versailles
       </a>
       , due to intense pressure from the student protesters and public opinion alike.
      </p>
      <p>
       The May Fourth Movement helped to rekindle the then-fading cause of republican revolution. In 1917
       <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">
        Sun Yat-sen
       </a>
       had become commander-in-chief of a rival military government in
       <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">
        Guangzhou
       </a>
       in collaboration with southern warlords. Sun's efforts to obtain aid from the Western democracies were ignored, however, and in 1920 he turned to the Soviet Union, which had recently achieved its own revolution. The Soviets sought to befriend the Chinese revolutionists by offering scathing attacks on Western imperialism. But for political expediency, the Soviet leadership initiated a dual policy of support for both Sun and the newly established
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Chinese Communist Party">
        Chinese Communist Party
       </a>
       (CCP).
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Kuomintang" title="Flag of the Kuomintang">
          flag of the Kuomintang
         </a>
         , one canton of the
         <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Flag of the Republic of China">
          flag of the Republic of China
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The policy of working with the
       <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">
        Kuomintang
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">
        Chiang Kai-shek
       </a>
       had been recommended by the
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
        Dutch
       </a>
       Communist
       <a href="/wiki/Henk_Sneevliet" title="Henk Sneevliet">
        Henk Sneevliet
       </a>
       , chosen in 1923 to be the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comintern" title="Comintern">
        Comintern
       </a>
       representative in China due to his revolutionary experience in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_Indies" title="Dutch Indies">
        Dutch Indies
       </a>
       , where he had a major role in founding the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Partai_Komunis_Indonesia" title="Partai Komunis Indonesia">
        Partai Komunis Indonesia
       </a>
       (PKI) – and who felt that the Chinese party was too small and weak to undertake a major effort on its own (see
       <a href="/wiki/Henk_Sneevliet#Working_for_the_Comintern" title="Henk Sneevliet">
        Henk Sneevliet's work for the Comintern
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       In early 1927, the Kuomintang-CCP rivalry led to a split in the revolutionary ranks. The CCP and the left wing of the Kuomintang had decided to move the seat of the Nationalist government from Guangzhou to
       <a href="/wiki/Wuhan" title="Wuhan">
        Wuhan
       </a>
       . But
       <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">
        Chiang Kai-shek
       </a>
       , whose
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Expedition" title="Northern Expedition">
        Northern Expedition
       </a>
       was proving successful, set his forces to destroying the Shanghai CCP apparatus and established an anti-Communist government at Nanjing in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/April_12_Incident" title="April 12 Incident">
        April 1927
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_1920s_and_the_Depression">
        The 1920s and the Depression
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: The 1920s and the Depression">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">
        Interwar period
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Roaring_Twenties" title="Roaring Twenties">
        Roaring Twenties
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
        Great Depression
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The interwar period was the period between the end of the First World War and the beginning of the Second World War. This period was marked by turmoil in much of the world, as Europe struggled to recover from the devastation of the First World War.
      </p>
      <p>
       In North America, especially the first half of this period, people experienced considerable prosperity in the Roaring Twenties. The social and societal upheaval known as the Roaring Twenties began in North America and spread to Europe in the
       <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_I" title="Aftermath of World War I">
        aftermath of World War I
       </a>
       . The
       <i>
        Roaring Twenties
       </i>
       , often called "
       <a href="/wiki/Jazz_Age" title="Jazz Age">
        The Jazz Age
       </a>
       ", saw an exposition of social, artistic, and cultural dynamism. '
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Normalcy" title="Normalcy">
        Normalcy
       </a>
       ' returned to politics,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jazz_music" title="Jazz music">
        jazz music
       </a>
       blossomed, the
       <a href="/wiki/Flapper" title="Flapper">
        flapper
       </a>
       redefined modern womanhood,
       <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">
        Art Deco
       </a>
       peaked. The spirit of the Roaring Twenties was marked by a general feeling of discontinuity associated with modernity, a break with traditions. Everything seemed to be feasible through modern technology. New technologies, especially automobiles, movies and radio proliferated 'modernity' to a large part of the population. The 1920s saw the general favor of practicality, in architecture as well as in daily life. The 1920s was further distinguished by several inventions and discoveries, extensive industrial growth and the rise in consumer demand and aspirations, and significant changes in
       <a href="/wiki/Lifestyle_(sociology)" title="Lifestyle (sociology)">
        lifestyle
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europe_in_1923.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5456" data-file-width="7097" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Europe_in_1923.jpg/300px-Europe_in_1923.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Europe_in_1923.jpg/450px-Europe_in_1923.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Europe_in_1923.jpg/600px-Europe_in_1923.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Europe_in_1923.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Europe between 1920 and 1938.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Europe spent these years rebuilding and coming to terms with the vast human cost of the conflict. The economy of the United States became increasingly intertwined with that of Europe. In Germany, the
       <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">
        Weimar Republic
       </a>
       gave way to episodes of political and economic turmoil, which culminated with the
       <a href="/wiki/Hyperinflation_in_the_Weimar_Republic" title="Hyperinflation in the Weimar Republic">
        German hyperinflation
       </a>
       of 1923 and the failed
       <a href="/wiki/Beer_Hall_Putsch" title="Beer Hall Putsch">
        Beer Hall Putsch
       </a>
       of that same year. When Germany could no longer afford war payments, Wall Street invested heavily in European debts to keep the European economy afloat as a large consumer market for American mass-produced goods. By the middle of the decade,
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">
        economic development
       </a>
       soared in Europe, and the Roaring Twenties broke out in Germany, Britain and France, the second half of the decade becoming known as the "
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_Twenties" title="Golden Twenties">
        Golden Twenties
       </a>
       ". In France and francophone Canada, they were also called the "
       <i>
        années folles
       </i>
       " ("Crazy Years").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Worldwide prosperity changed dramatically with the onset of the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
        Great Depression
       </a>
       in 1929. The
       <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929" title="Wall Street Crash of 1929">
        Wall Street Crash of 1929
       </a>
       served to punctuate the end of the previous era, as
       <i>
        The Great Depression
       </i>
       set in. The
       <i>
        Great Depression
       </i>
       was a worldwide economic
       <a href="/wiki/Recession" title="Recession">
        downturn
       </a>
