       starting in most places in 1929 and ending at different times in the 1930s or early 1940s for different countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CRomer1_108-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CRomer1-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was the largest and most important
       <a href="/wiki/Depression_(economics)" title="Depression (economics)">
        economic depression
       </a>
       in the 20th century, and is used in the 21st century as an example of how far the world's economy can fall.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The depression had devastating effects in virtually every country, rich or poor. International trade plunged by half to two-thirds, as did personal income, tax revenue, prices and profits.
       <a href="/wiki/Cities_in_the_Great_Depression" title="Cities in the Great Depression">
        Cities all around the world
       </a>
       were hit hard, especially those dependent on
       <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">
        heavy industry
       </a>
       . Construction was virtually halted in many countries. Farming and rural areas suffered as crop prices fell by roughly 60 percent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USBLS_110-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-USBLS-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
        <a href="#cite_note-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Facing plummeting demand with few alternate sources of jobs, areas dependent on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_sector_of_economic_activity" title="Primary sector of economic activity">
        primary sector industries
       </a>
       suffered the most.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Great Depression ended at different times in different countries with the
       <a href="/wiki/Home_front_during_World_War_II" title="Home front during World War II">
        effect lasting into the next era
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       America's Great Depression ended in 1941 with America's entry into World War II.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The majority of countries set up relief programs, and most underwent some sort of political upheaval, pushing them to the left or right. In some world states, the desperate citizens turned toward nationalist
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demagogy" title="Demagogy">
        demagogues
       </a>
       —the most infamous being
       <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">
        Adolf Hitler
       </a>
       —setting the stage for the next era of war. The convulsion brought on by the worldwide depression resulted in the rise of
       <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">
        Nazism
       </a>
       . In Asia, Japan became an ever more assertive power, especially with regards to China.
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nanjing_period">
        Nanjing period
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Nanjing period">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_decade" title="Nanjing decade">
        Nanjing decade
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sino-german_cooperation.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="553" data-file-width="600" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sino-german_cooperation.png/220px-Sino-german_cooperation.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sino-german_cooperation.png/330px-Sino-german_cooperation.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sino-german_cooperation.png/440px-Sino-german_cooperation.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sino-german_cooperation.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         With
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sino-German_cooperation_until_1941" title="Sino-German cooperation until 1941">
          Sino-German cooperation until 1941
         </a>
         , Chinese industry and military was improved just prior to the war against Japan.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The "Nanjing Decade" of 1928–37 was one of consolidation and accomplishment under the leadership of the Nationalists, with a mixed but generally positive record in the economy, social progress, development of
       <a href="/wiki/Democracy_in_China" title="Democracy in China">
        democracy
       </a>
       , and cultural creativity. Some of the harsh aspects of foreign concessions and privileges in China were moderated through diplomacy.
      </p>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sino-German_cooperation_until_1941" title="Sino-German cooperation until 1941">
        Sino-German cooperation until 1941
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/National_Resources_Commission" title="National Resources Commission">
        National Resources Commission
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">
        Chinese Civil War
       </a>
      </div>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_League_and_crises">
        The League and crises
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: The League and crises">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <p>
       The interwar period was also marked by a radical change in the international order, away from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balance_of_power_in_international_relations" title="Balance of power in international relations">
        balance of power
       </a>
       that had dominated pre–World War I Europe. One main institution that was meant to bring stability was the
       <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
        League of Nations
       </a>
       , which was created after the First World War with the intention of maintaining world security and peace and encouraging economic growth between member countries. The League was undermined by the bellicosity of
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Nazi Germany
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Japan" title="Imperial Japan">
        Imperial Japan
       </a>
       , the Soviet Union, and
       <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">
        Mussolini's
       </a>
       Italy, and by the non-participation of the United States, leading many to question its effectiveness and legitimacy.
      </p>
      <p>
       A series of international crises strained the League to its limits, the earliest being the
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Japanese invasion of Manchuria">
        invasion of Manchuria
       </a>
       by Japan and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abyssinian_crisis" title="Abyssinian crisis">
        Abyssinian crisis
       </a>
       of 1935/36 in which Italy invaded
       <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Empire" title="Ethiopian Empire">
        Abyssinia
       </a>
       , one of the only free African nations at that time. The League tried to enforce economic sanctions upon Italy, but to no avail. The incident highlighted French and British weakness, exemplified by their reluctance to alienate Italy and lose her as their ally. The limited actions taken by the Western powers pushed Mussolini's Italy towards alliance with Hitler's Germany anyway. The Abyssinian war showed Hitler how weak the League was and encouraged the remilitarization of the Rhineland in flagrant disregard of the Treaty of Versailles. This was the first in a series of provocative acts culminating in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland_(1939)" title="Invasion of Poland (1939)">
        invasion of Poland
       </a>
       in September 1939 and the beginning of the Second World War.
      </p>
      <p>
       Few Chinese had any illusions about Japanese designs on China. Hungry for raw materials and pressed by a growing population, Japan initiated the seizure of
       <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">
        Manchuria
       </a>
       in September 1931 and established ex-Qing emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Puyi" title="Puyi">
        Puyi
       </a>
       as head of the
       <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">
        puppet state
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Manchukuo" title="Manchukuo">
        Manchukuo
       </a>
       in 1932. During the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sino-Japanese_War_(1937%E2%80%931945)" title="Sino-Japanese War (1937–1945)">
        Sino-Japanese War (1937–1945)
       </a>
       , the loss of Manchuria, and its vast potential for industrial development and war industries, was a blow to the Kuomintang economy. The
       <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
        League of Nations
       </a>
       , established at the end of World War I, was unable to act in the face of the Japanese defiance. After 1940, conflicts between the Kuomintang and Communists became more frequent in the
       <a href="/wiki/Free_China_(Second_Sino-Japanese_War)" title="Free China (Second Sino-Japanese War)">
        areas not under Japanese control
       </a>
       . The Communists expanded their influence wherever opportunities presented themselves through mass organizations, administrative reforms, and the land- and tax-reform measures favoring the peasants—while the Kuomintang attempted to neutralize the spread of Communist influence.
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tripartite_Pact">
        Tripartite Pact
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Tripartite Pact">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">
        Second Sino-Japanese War
       </a>
       had seen tensions rise between Imperial Japan and the United States; events such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panay_incident" title="Panay incident">
        Panay incident
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Nanking_Massacre" title="Nanking Massacre">
        Nanking Massacre
       </a>
       turned American public opinion against Japan. With the occupation of
       <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">
        French Indochina
       </a>
       in the years of 1940–41, and with the continuing war in China, the United States placed embargoes on Japan of
       <a href="/wiki/Strategic_material" title="Strategic material">
        strategic materials
       </a>
       such as scrap metal and oil, which were vitally needed for the war effort. The Japanese were faced with the option of either withdrawing from China and losing face or seizing and securing new sources of raw materials in the resource-rich, European-controlled colonies of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_East_Asia" title="South East Asia">
        South East Asia
       </a>
       —specifically
       <a href="/wiki/British_Malaya" title="British Malaya">
        British Malaya
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">
        Dutch East Indies
       </a>
       (modern-day
       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
        Indonesia
       </a>
       ). In 1940, Imperial Japan signed the
       <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">
        Tripartite Pact
       </a>
       with Nazi Germany and Fascist Italy.
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">
        World War II
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: World War II">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_German_Reich_(1935%E2%80%931945).svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Flag_of_the_German_Reich_%281935%E2%80%931945%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_German_Reich_%281935%E2%80%931945%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Flag_of_the_German_Reich_%281935%E2%80%931945%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_German_Reich_%281935%E2%80%931945%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Flag_of_the_German_Reich_%281935%E2%80%931945%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_German_Reich_%281935%E2%80%931945%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_German_Reich_(1935%E2%80%931945).svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         National flag of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_Reich" title="Third Reich">
          Third Reich
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
          Nazi Germany
         </a>
         ).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Second World War was a global military conflict that took place in 1939–1945. It was the largest and deadliest war in history, culminating in
       <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">
        the Holocaust
       </a>
       and ending with the dropping of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atom_bomb" title="Atom bomb">
        atom bomb
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Even though Japan had been fighting in China since 1937, the conventional view is that the war began on September 1, 1939, when
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Nazi Germany
       </a>
       invaded Poland, the
       <a href="/wiki/Drang_nach_Osten" title="Drang nach Osten">
        Drang nach Osten
       </a>
       . Within two days the United Kingdom and France declared war on Germany, even though the fighting was confined to Poland. Pursuant to a then-secret provision of its non-aggression
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molotov-Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact">
        Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact
       </a>
       , the Soviet Union joined with Germany on September 17, 1939, to conquer Poland and to divide Eastern Europe.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">
        Allies
       </a>
       were initially made up of Poland, the United Kingdom, France, Australia, Canada, New Zealand, South Africa, as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">
        British Commonwealth
       </a>
       countries which were controlled directly by the UK, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">
        Indian Empire
       </a>
       . All of these countries declared war on Germany in September 1939.
      </p>
      <p>
       Following the lull in fighting, known as the "
       <a href="/wiki/Phoney_War" title="Phoney War">
        Phoney War
       </a>
       ", Germany invaded western Europe in May 1940. Six weeks later, France, in the mean time attacked by Italy as well, surrendered to Germany, which then tried unsuccessfully to conquer Britain. On September 27, Germany, Italy, and Japan signed a mutual defense agreement, the
       <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">
        Tripartite Pact
       </a>
       , and were known as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" title="Axis Powers">
        Axis Powers
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Naval_Ensign_of_Japan.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Naval_Ensign_of_Japan.svg/220px-Naval_Ensign_of_Japan.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Naval_Ensign_of_Japan.svg/330px-Naval_Ensign_of_Japan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Naval_Ensign_of_Japan.svg/440px-Naval_Ensign_of_Japan.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Naval_Ensign_of_Japan.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rising_sun_flag" title="Rising sun flag">
          Ensign of the Imperial Japanese Navy
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Nine months later, on June 22, 1941, Germany launched a massive invasion of the Soviet Union, which promptly joined the Allies. Germany was now engaged in fighting a war on two fronts. This proved to be a mistake by Germany – Germany had not successfully carried out the invasion of Britain and the war turned against the Axis.
      </p>
      <p>
       On December 7, 1941,
       <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">
        Japan attacked the United States at Pearl Harbor
       </a>
       , bringing it too into the war on the Allied side. China also joined the Allies, as eventually did most of the rest of the world. China was in turmoil at the time, and attacked Japanese armies through guerilla-type warfare. By the beginning of 1942, the major combatants were aligned as follows: the British Commonwealth, the United States, and the Soviet Union were fighting Germany and Italy; and the British Commonwealth, China, and the United States were fighting Japan. The United Kingdom, the United States, the Soviet Union and China were referred as a "trusteeship of the powerful" during the
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Justus_115-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Justus-115">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and were recognized as the Allied "Big Four" in
       <a href="/wiki/Declaration_by_United_Nations" title="Declaration by United Nations">
        Declaration by United Nations
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
        <a href="#cite_note-116">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These four countries were considered as the "
       <a href="/wiki/Four_Policemen" title="Four Policemen">
        Four Policemen
       </a>
       " or "Four Sheriffs" of the
       <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">
        Allies power
       </a>
       and primary victors of World War II.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From then through August 1945, battles raged across all of Europe, in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Ocean" title="North Atlantic Ocean">
        North Atlantic Ocean
       </a>
       , across North Africa, throughout
       <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">
        Southeast Asia
       </a>
       , throughout China, across the Pacific Ocean and in the air over Japan.
      </p>
      <p>
       Italy surrendered in September 1943 and was split into a northern Germany-occupied
       <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">
        puppet state
       </a>
       and an Allies-friendly state in the South; Germany surrendered in May 1945. Following the
       <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">
        atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">
        Japan surrendered
       </a>
       , marking the end of the war on September 2, 1945.
      </p>
      <p>
       It is possible that around 62 million people
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties" title="World War II casualties">
        died in the war
       </a>
       ; estimates vary greatly. About 60% of all casualties were civilians, who died as a result of disease, starvation,
       <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
        genocide
       </a>
       (in particular, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocaust" title="Holocaust">
        Holocaust
       </a>
       ), and aerial bombing. The former Soviet Union and China suffered the most casualties. Estimates place deaths in the Soviet Union at around 23 million, while China suffered about 10 million. No country lost a greater portion of its population than Poland: approximately 5.6 million, or 16%, of its pre-war population of 34.8 million died.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Italy_(1861-1946).svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Flag_of_Italy_%281861-1946%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Italy_%281861-1946%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Flag_of_Italy_%281861-1946%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Italy_%281861-1946%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Flag_of_Italy_%281861-1946%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Italy_%281861-1946%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Italy_(1861-1946).svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Flag of the
         <a href="/wiki/Italian_Empire" title="Italian Empire">
          Italian Empire
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Holocaust (which roughly means "burnt whole") was the deliberate and systematic murder of millions of Jews and other "unwanted" during World War II by the Nazi regime in Germany. Several differing views exist regarding whether it was intended to occur from the war's beginning, or if the plans for it came about later. Regardless, persecution of Jews extended well before the war even started, such as in the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">
         Kristallnacht
        </a>
       </i>
       (Night of Broken Glass). The Nazis used propaganda to great effect to stir up anti-Semitic feelings within ordinary Germans.
      </p>
      <p>
       After World War II, Europe was informally split into Western and Soviet
       <a href="/wiki/Sphere_of_influence" title="Sphere of influence">
        spheres of influence
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">
        Western Europe
       </a>
       later aligned as the
       <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">
        North Atlantic Treaty Organization
       </a>
       (NATO) and
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">
        Eastern Europe
       </a>
       as the
       <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">
        Warsaw Pact
       </a>
       . There was a shift in power from Western Europe and the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
        British Empire
       </a>
       to the two new superpowers, the United States and the Soviet Union. These two rivals would later face off in the
       <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">
        Cold War
       </a>
       . In Asia, the defeat of Japan led to its
       <a href="/wiki/Democratization" title="Democratization">
        democratization
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">
        China's civil war
       </a>
       continued through and after the war, resulting eventually in the establishment of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">
        People's Republic of China
       </a>
       . The former colonies of the European powers began their road to independence.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-1945_world">
        Post-1945 world
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Post-1945 world">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3002" data-file-width="3000" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/220px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/330px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/440px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/The_Blue_Marble" title="The Blue Marble">
           The Blue Marble
          </a>
         </i>
         , a photograph of Earth as seen from Apollo 17. The second half of the 20th century saw an increase of interest in both
         <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">
          space exploration
         </a>
         and the
         <a href="/wiki/Environmental_movement" title="Environmental movement">
          environmental movement
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The mid-20th century is distinguished from most of human history in that its most significant changes were directly or indirectly economic and technological in nature. Economic development was the force behind vast changes in everyday life, to a degree which was unprecedented in human history.
      </p>
      <p>
       Over the course of the 20th century, the world's per-capita
       <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">
        gross domestic product
       </a>
       grew by a factor of five,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       much more than all earlier centuries combined (including the 19th with its Industrial Revolution). Many economists make the case that this understates the magnitude of growth, as many of the goods and services consumed at the end of the 20th century, such as improved medicine (causing world life expectancy to increase by more than two decades) and communications technologies, were not available at any price at its beginning. However, the gulf between the world's rich and poor grew wider,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the majority of the global population remained in the poor side of the divide.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Still, advancing technology and medicine has had a great impact even in the
       <a href="/wiki/Global_South" title="Global South">
        Global South
       </a>
       . Large-scale industry and more centralized
       <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">
        media
       </a>
       made brutal dictatorships possible on an unprecedented scale in the middle of the century, leading to wars that were also unprecedented. However, the increased communications contributed to
       <a href="/wiki/Democratization" title="Democratization">
        democratization
       </a>
       . Technological developments included the development of airplanes and
       <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">
        space exploration
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_technology" title="Nuclear technology">
        nuclear technology
       </a>
       , advancement in
       <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">
        genetics
       </a>
       , and the dawning of the
       <a href="/wiki/Information_Age" title="Information Age">
        Information Age
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="American_Peace">
        American Peace
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: American Peace">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Pax_Americana" title="Pax Americana">
        Pax Americana
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_States.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_States.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         National flag of the United States.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Pax Americana is an appellation applied to the historical concept of relative liberal peace in the Western world, resulting from the preponderance of power enjoyed by the United States of America starting around the start of the 20th century. Although the term finds its primary utility in the latter half of the 20th century, it has been used in various places and eras. Its modern connotations concern the peace established after the end of World War II in 1945.
      </p>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       For more details on this topic, see
       <a href="/wiki/American_Century" title="American Century">
        American Century
       </a>
       .
      </div>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War_era">
        Cold War era
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Cold War era">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">
        Cold War
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Cold War began in the mid-1940s and lasted into the early 1990s. Throughout this period, the conflict was expressed through military coalitions, espionage, weapons development, invasions, propaganda, and competitive technological development. The conflict included costly defense spending, a massive
       <a href="/wiki/Conventional_weapon" title="Conventional weapon">
        conventional
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">
        nuclear
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Arms_race" title="Arms race">
        arms race
       </a>
       , and numerous
       <a href="/wiki/Proxy_war" title="Proxy war">
        proxy wars
       </a>
       ; the two
       <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">
        superpowers
       </a>
       never fought one another directly.
      </p>
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NATO_vs._Warsaw_(1949-1990).svg">
          <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="1600" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/NATO_vs._Warsaw_%281949-1990%29.svg/750px-NATO_vs._Warsaw_%281949-1990%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/NATO_vs._Warsaw_%281949-1990%29.svg/1125px-NATO_vs._Warsaw_%281949-1990%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/NATO_vs._Warsaw_%281949-1990%29.svg/1500px-NATO_vs._Warsaw_%281949-1990%29.svg.png 2x" width="750"/>
         </a>
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NATO_vs._Warsaw_(1949-1990).svg" title="Enlarge">
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
           Borders of
           <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">
            NATO
           </a>
           (blue) and
           <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">
            Warsaw Pact
           </a>
           (red) states during the Cold war era.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Soviet Union created the
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">
        Eastern Bloc
       </a>
       of countries that it occupied, annexing some as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Socialist_Republics" title="Soviet Socialist Republics">
        Soviet Socialist Republics
       </a>
       and maintaining others as satellite states that would later form the
       <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">
        Warsaw Pact
       </a>
       . The United States and various western European countries began a policy of "
       <a href="/wiki/Containment" title="Containment">
        containment
       </a>
       " of
       <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">
        communism
       </a>
       and forged myriad alliances to this end, including
       <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">
        NATO
       </a>
       . Several of these western countries also coordinated efforts regarding the rebuilding of western Europe, including western Germany, which the Soviets opposed. In other regions of the world, such as Latin America and
       <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">
        Southeast Asia
       </a>
       , the Soviet Union fostered
       <a href="/wiki/Communist_revolution" title="Communist revolution">
        communist revolutionary
       </a>
       movements, which the United States and many of its allies opposed and, in some cases, attempted to "
       <a href="/wiki/Rollback" title="Rollback">
        roll back
       </a>
       ". Many countries were prompted to align themselves with the nations that would later form either NATO or the Warsaw Pact, though other movements would also emerge.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Cold War saw periods of both heightened tension and relative calm. International crises arose, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Blockade" title="Berlin Blockade">
        Berlin Blockade
       </a>
       (1948–1949), the
       <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">
        Korean War
       </a>
       (1950–1953), the
       <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Crisis_of_1961" title="Berlin Crisis of 1961">
        Berlin Crisis of 1961
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">
        Vietnam War
       </a>
       (1955–1975), the
       <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">
        Cuban Missile Crisis
       </a>
       (1962), the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_war_in_Afghanistan" title="Soviet war in Afghanistan">
        Soviet war in Afghanistan
       </a>
       (1979–1989) and
       <a href="/wiki/Able_Archer_83" title="Able Archer 83">
        NATO exercises in November 1983
       </a>
       . There were also periods of reduced tension as both sides sought
       <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9tente" title="Détente">
        détente
       </a>
       . Direct military attacks on adversaries were deterred by the potential for
       <a href="/wiki/Mutual_assured_destruction" title="Mutual assured destruction">
        mutual assured destruction
       </a>
       using deliverable
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">
        nuclear weapons
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <table style="margin:auto;">
       <tr>
        <td>
         <div class="thumb tright">
          <div class="thumbinner" style="width:264px;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europe_1988.png">
            <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="262" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/63/Europe_1988.png" width="262"/>
           </a>
           <div class="thumbcaption">
            <div class="magnify">
             <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Europe_1988.png" title="Enlarge">
             </a>
            </div>
            European
            <a href="/wiki/Trade_bloc" title="Trade bloc">
             trade blocs
            </a>
            as of the late 1980s. EEC member states are marked in blue,
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EFTA" title="EFTA">
             EFTA
            </a>
            – green, and Comecon – red.
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td>
         <div class="thumb tright">
          <div class="thumbinner" style="width:335px;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cold_War_Map_1980.svg">
            <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="477" data-file-width="940" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cold_War_Map_1980.svg/333px-Cold_War_Map_1980.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cold_War_Map_1980.svg/500px-Cold_War_Map_1980.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cold_War_Map_1980.svg/666px-Cold_War_Map_1980.svg.png 2x" width="333"/>
           </a>
           <div class="thumbcaption">
            <div class="magnify">
             <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cold_War_Map_1980.svg" title="Enlarge">
             </a>
            </div>
            East and West in 1980, as defined by the Cold War. The Cold War had divided Europe politically into East and West, with the Iron Curtain splitting
            <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">
             Central Europe
            </a>
            .
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The Cold War drew to a close in the late 1980s and the early 1990s. The United States under President
       <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">
        Ronald Reagan
       </a>
       increased diplomatic, military, and economic pressure on the Soviet Union, which was already suffering from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brezhnev_stagnation" title="Brezhnev stagnation">
        severe economic stagnation
       </a>
       . In the second half of the 1980s, newly appointed Soviet leader
       <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">
        Mikhail Gorbachev
       </a>
       introduced the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">
         perestroika
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">
         glasnost
        </a>
       </i>
       reforms.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1985%E2%80%931991)" title="History of the Soviet Union (1985–1991)">
        The Soviet Union collapsed
       </a>
       in 1991, leaving the United States as the dominant military power, though Russia retained much of the massive Soviet nuclear arsenal.
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America_polarization">
        Latin America polarization
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Latin America polarization">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <p>
       In Latin America in the 1970s, leftists acquired a significant political influence which prompted the right-wing, ecclesiastical authorities and a large portion of the individual country's upper class to support coups d'état to avoid what they perceived as a communist threat. This was further fueled by Cuban and United States intervention which led to a political polarization. Most South American countries were in some periods ruled by
       <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">
        military dictatorships
       </a>
       that were supported by the United States of America. In the 1970s, the regimes of the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">
        Southern Cone
       </a>
       collaborated in
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Condor" title="Operation Condor">
        Operation Condor
       </a>
       killing many
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leftist" title="Leftist">
        leftist
       </a>
       dissidents, including some
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_guerrilla" title="Urban guerrilla">
        urban guerrillas
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, by the early 1990s all countries had restored their democracies.
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Space_Age">
        Space Age
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: Space Age">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6200" data-file-width="6200" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg/275px-Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg/413px-Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg/550px-Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg 2x" width="275"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hubble_ultra_deep_field_high_rez_edit1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         This high-resolution image of the Hubble Ultra Deep Field includes galaxies of various ages, sizes, shapes, and colors. The smallest, reddest galaxies, are some of the most distant galaxies to have been imaged by an optical telescope
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Space_Age" title="Space Age">
        Space Age
       </a>
       is a period encompassing the activities related to the
       <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">
        Space Race
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">
        space exploration
       </a>
       , space technology, and the cultural developments influenced by these events. The Space Age began with the development of several technologies that culminated with the launch of
       <a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">
        Sputnik 1
       </a>
       by the Soviet Union in October 1957. This was the world's first artificial satellite, orbiting the Earth in 98.1 minutes and weighing in at 83 kg. The launch of Sputnik 1 ushered a new era of political, scientific and technological achievements that became known as the Space Age. The Space Age was characterized by rapid development of new technology in a close race mostly between the United States and the Soviet Union. The Space Age brought the first human spaceflight during the
       <a href="/wiki/Vostok_programme" title="Vostok programme">
        Vostok programme
       </a>
       and reached its peak with the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">
        Apollo program
       </a>
       which captured the imagination of much of the world's population. The landing of
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">
        Apollo 11
       </a>
       was an event watched by over 500 million people around the world and is widely recognized as one of the defining moments of the 20th century. Since then and with the end of the space race due to the
       <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">
        dissolution of the Soviet Union
       </a>
       , public attention has largely moved to other areas.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_schools">
        Education and schools
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Education and schools">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">
        humanities
       </a>
       are academic disciplines which study the
       <a href="/wiki/Human_condition" title="Human condition">
        human condition
       </a>
       , using methods that are primarily
       <a href="/wiki/Analytic_induction" title="Analytic induction">
        analytic
       </a>
       , critical, or speculative, as distinguished from the mainly
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empirical" title="Empirical">
        empirical
       </a>
       approaches of the
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_science" title="Natural science">
        natural
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_sciences" title="Social sciences">
        social sciences
       </a>
       . Although many of the subjects of modern history coincide with that of standard history, the subject is taught independently by various systems of education in the world.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="British_education">
        British education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: British education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Students can choose the subject at university. The material covered includes from the mid-18th century, to analysis of the present day. Virtually all colleges and sixth forms that do teach modern history do it alongside standard history; very few teach the subject exclusively.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Universities">
        Universities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_history&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Universities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       At the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">
        University of Oxford
       </a>
       'Modern History' has a somewhat different meaning. The contrast is not with the Middle Ages but with Antiquity. The earliest period that can be studied in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Final_Honour_School" title="Final Honour School">
        Final Honour School
       </a>
       of Modern History begins in 285.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>

        <li id="cite_note-89">

            ^

         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation book">
           <i>
            Compact Oxford English Dictionary
           </i>
           . Oxford University Press. 2007.
           <q>
            humanism
            <i>
             n.
            </i>
            1 a rationalistic system of thought attaching prime importance to human rather than divine or supernatural matters. 2 a Renaissance cultural movement that turned away from medieval scholastic-ism and revived interest in ancient Greek and Roman thought.
           </q>
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Compact+Oxford+English+Dictionary&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AModern+history">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
          Typically, abridgments of this definition omit all senses except #1, such as in the
          <a class="external text" href="http://dictionary.cambridge.org/define.asp?key=38402&amp;dict=CALD" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            Cambridge Advanced Learner's Dictionary
           </i>
          </a>
          ,
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.thefreedictionary.com/humanism" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            Collins Essential English Dictionary
           </i>
          </a>
          , and
          <cite class="citation book">
           <i>
            Webster's Concise Dictionary
           </i>
           . New York: RHR Press. 2001. p. 177.
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Webster%27s+Concise+Dictionary&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pages=177&amp;rft.pub=RHR+Press&amp;rft.date=2001&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AModern+history">

           </span>
          </span>
         </span>

        <li id="cite_note-91">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-91">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          In the 1888 English edition of the
          <i>
           Communist Manifest
          </i>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Engels" title="Friedrich Engels">
           Friedrich Engels
          </a>
          added a footnote with the commentary: "That is, all written history. In 1847, the prehistory of society, the social organization existing previous to recorded history, was all but unknown. Since then Haxthausen discovered common ownership of land In Russia, Maurer concluded it to be the social foundation from which all Teutonic races started in history, and by and by village communities were found to be, or to have been, the primitive form of society everywhere from India to Ireland. The Inner organization of this primitive Communistic society was laid bare, In its typical form, by Morgan's work on the true nature of the gens and Its relation to the tribe. With the dissolution of these primaeval communities society begins to be differentiated into separate and finally antagonistic classes. I have attempte to retrace this process of dissolution in "
          <i>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Der_Ursprung_der_Familie,_des_Privateigenthums_und_des_Staats" title="Der Ursprung der Familie, des Privateigenthums und des Staats">
            Der Ursprung der Familie, des Privateigenthums und des Staats
           </a>
          </i>
          "", from Marx, Karl, Friedrich Engels, Leon Trotsky, and Karl Marx.
          <i>
           <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=dEyEzazZKwIC&amp;pg=PA46" rel="nofollow">
            The Communist Manifesto and Its Relevance for Today
           </a>
          </i>
          . Chippendale, N.S.W.: Resistance Books, 1998. p. 46, see also
          <i>
           <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=p7s0oTEWB_MC&amp;pg=PA204" rel="nofollow">
            Cornelius Castoriadis, Political and Social Writings
           </a>
          </i>
          . Minneapolis: University of Minnesota Press, 1993. p. 204
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-92">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-92">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          Marx makes no claim to have produced a master key to history. Historical materialism is not "an historico-philosophic theory of the marche generale imposed by fate upon every people, whatever the historic circumstances in which it finds itself". (Marx, Karl, Letter to editor of the Russian paper
          <i>
           Otetchestvennye Zapiskym
          </i>
          , 1877) His ideas, he explains, are based on a concrete study of the actual conditions that pertained in Europe.
         </span>

        : Crash Course World History #34 – YouTube
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=alJaltUmrGo" rel="nofollow">
         Imperialism
        </a>
        : Crash Course World History #35 – YouTube
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_XPZQ0LAlR4" rel="nofollow">
         Archdukes, Cynicism, and World War I
        </a>
        : Crash Course World History #36 – YouTube
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UUCEeC4f6ts" rel="nofollow">
         Communists, Nationalists, and China's Revolutions
        </a>
        : Crash Course World History #37 – YouTube
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q78COTwT7nE" rel="nofollow">
         World War II
        </a>
        : Crash Course World History #38 – YouTube
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=y9HjvHZfCUI" rel="nofollow">
         USA vs USSR Fight
        </a>
        ! The Cold War: Crash Course World History #39 – YouTube
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=T_sGTspaF4Y" rel="nofollow">
         Decolonization and Nationalism Triumphant
        </a>
        : Crash Course World History #40 – YouTube
       </li>
      </ul>

        <tr>
         <th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="text-align:center;;width:1%;background: #F5F5DC">
          Eight thresholds
         </th>
         <td class="navbox-list navbox-even" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
          <div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
           <ul>
            <li>
             1:
             <b>
              Creation
             </b>
             -
             <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">
              Big Bang
             </a>
             and
             <a href="/wiki/Cosmogony" title="Cosmogony">
              cosmogony
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             2:
             <b>
              Stars
             </b>
             -
             <a href="/wiki/Star" title="Star">
              creation of stars
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             3:
             <b>
              Elements
             </b>
             -
             <a href="/wiki/Chemical_element" title="Chemical element">
              creation of chemical elements
             </a>
             inside
             <a href="/wiki/Stellar_evolution" title="Stellar evolution">
              dying stars
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             4:
             <b>
              Planets
             </b>
             -
             <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">
              formation of planets
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             5:
             <b>
              Life
             </b>
             -
             <a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis" title="Abiogenesis">
              abiogenesis
             </a>
             and
             <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">
              evolution
             </a>
             of
             <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">
              life
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             6:
             <b>
              Humans
             </b>
             - development of
             <i>
              <a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">
               Homo sapiens
              </a>
             </i>
             <ul>
              <li>
               <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">
                Paleolithic era
               </a>
              </li>
             </ul>
            </li>
            <li>
             7:
             <b>
              Agriculture
             </b>
             -
             <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">
              Agricultural Revolution
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
             8:
             <b>
              Modernity
             </b>
             -
             <a class="mw-selflink selflink">
              modern era
             </a>
            </li>
           </ul>
          </div>
